            text: >-
              In the realm of functional genomics, a critical gap exists in
              understanding how gene expression patterns underpin complex traits
              and influence disease etiology, which is essential for identifying
              therapeutic targets and facilitating drug repurposing. While
              individual genes have been the focus of genetic studies, the
              collective action of gene modules in specific cellular contexts
              remains underexplored. Here we present PhenoPLIER, a novel
              computational framework that leverages gene co-expression patterns
              to elucidate the genetic basis of diseases and predict drug
              mechanisms. Our study demonstrates that disease-associated gene
              modules, expressed in relevant cell types, are significantly
              correlated with complex traits. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
              known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action, as
              evidenced by our CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation, which
              highlights functionally important genes that lack direct
              associations yet are prioritized within trait-associated modules.
              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER advances our ability to interpret
              genetic associations beyond single-gene analyses, offering a more
              comprehensive understanding of disease etiology and uncovering
              potential therapeutic targets that may be overlooked by
              conventional methods. This approach has broad implications for the
              clustering of complex traits and the identification of novel drug
              repurposing opportunities.

              Genes operate synergistically within specific contexts to fulfill
              their biological roles. A mechanistic comprehension of gene
              expression regulation under varying conditions is essential for
              elucidating the influence of these genes on complex traits, a
              process pivotal for the innovation of novel therapeutics.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
              contributions of individual genes to disease mechanisms.
              Nonetheless, contemporary models suggest that gene-gene
              interactions are fundamental to the etiology and progression of
              complex diseases. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a novel
              computational methodology that integrates gene-trait associations
              with pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent
              framework for combined analysis. This framework is constructed
              upon clusters of co-expressed genes under identical conditions.
              Our findings reveal that disease states are significantly linked
              to gene clusters expressed in pertinent cell types. PhenoPLIER
              demonstrates precision in identifying established drug-disease
              relationships and deducing drug action mechanisms. Additionally, a
              CRISPR screen investigating lipid regulation highlighted that
              genes lacking direct associations can be critical and are
              identified within trait-associated gene clusters by PhenoPLIER,
              underscoring its potential in pinpointing therapeutic targets and
              facilitating drug repurposing.

              While transcriptome-wide association studies have advanced our
              understanding of individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, the
              complex interplay of gene-gene interactions in disease etiology
              and progression remains less explored. This gap hinders the
              development of new therapies that could target these interactions.
              Here we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
              leverages gene expression patterns to elucidate the genetic
              architecture of complex traits and identify potential therapeutic
              targets. By integrating gene-trait associations with
              pharmacological data, PhenoPLIER constructs a latent space where
              gene modules with coherent expression profiles are associated with
              diseases and drug responses. Our results demonstrate that disease
              traits are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in
              relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
              drug-disease relationships and provides insights into drug
              mechanisms of action. Additionally, a CRISPR screen for lipid
              regulation reveals that while some functionally important genes
              may not show direct associations, they are implicated in disease
              through their presence in trait-associated modules. In conclusion,
              PhenoPLIER not only sheds light on the underlying genetic factors
              of complex diseases but also offers a promising avenue for drug
              repurposing and the identification of novel therapeutic targets,
              thereby advancing the fields of functional genomics and precision
              medicine.

            Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform
            their functions. Determining how these genes influence complex

            association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
            in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the

            play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we

            our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and

            namedScores: *ref_49
            text: >-
              Genes operate synergistically within specific contexts to fulfill
              their biological roles. A mechanistic comprehension of gene
              expression regulation under varying conditions is essential for
              elucidating the influence of genes on complex traits, a
              cornerstone in the development of novel therapeutic interventions.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
              contributions of individual genes to disease mechanisms.
              Nonetheless, contemporary models suggest that gene-gene
              interactions are pivotal in the etiology and progression of
              complex diseases. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, an
              innovative computational methodology that integrates gene-trait
              associations with pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
              latent space for combined analysis. This latent space is
              constructed from clusters of co-expressed genes under identical
              conditions. Our findings reveal that disease states are
              significantly linked to gene clusters expressed in pertinent cell
              types. PhenoPLIER demonstrates precision in identifying
              established drug-disease relationships and elucidating drug
              mechanisms of action. Additionally, a CRISPR screen investigating
              lipid regulation highlighted that genes lacking direct
              associations can be critical, yet are identified within
              trait-associated gene clusters by PhenoPLIER, underscoring its
              potential in pinpointing therapeutic targets.

              Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
              contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
              influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
              expression regulation across different conditions. It has been
              shown that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.

            text: >-
              While transcriptome-wide association studies have advanced our
              understanding of individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, the
              complex interplay of gene-gene interactions in disease etiology
              and progression remains underexplored. This gap hinders the
              development of new therapies and the repurposing of existing
              drugs. Here we present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach
              that leverages gene expression patterns to elucidate the genetic
              architecture of complex traits and identify therapeutic targets.
              By integrating gene-trait associations with pharmacological data,
              PhenoPLIER constructs a latent space where diseases and drugs
              converge on shared gene expression modules, revealing cellular
              contexts pertinent to disease states. Our results demonstrate that
              PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease relationships
              and infers drugs' mechanisms of action. Notably, it also
              identifies key regulatory genes that, despite lacking direct
              associations with traits, are implicated in disease-relevant
              pathways through their module membership. In conclusion,
              PhenoPLIER provides a powerful framework for understanding disease
              etiology and identifying potential drug mechanisms, thereby
              offering a promising avenue for drug repurposing and the discovery
              of novel therapeutic targets. This approach advances the field of
              functional genomics by clustering complex traits and illuminating
              the underlying molecular interactions that drive disease.

              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is

              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There

              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,

              mechanisms of action. Additionally, our approach successfully
              identifies key regulatory genes in lipid metabolism that are not
              directly associated with traits but are highlighted within
              trait-associated modules, as demonstrated by a CRISPR screen. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER not only sheds light on the genetic
              underpinnings of complex diseases but also offers a powerful tool
              for identifying therapeutic targets and opportunities for drug
              repurposing, thereby advancing the fields of functional genomics
              and precision medicine.
